(106907): Misc. [New Tag]
OLD	¦ This particle may serve to give emphasis, like <s>id</s> and <s>eva</s>, especially after prepositions or demonstrative pronouns, in conjunction with <s>nu</s>, <s>vai</s>, <s>hi</s>, <s>cid</s>, &c. (<ab>e.g.</ab> <s>ayám u vām purutámo</s> … <s>johavīti</s> [<ls>RV. iii, 62, 2</ls>], this very person [your worshipper] invokes you &c.) It is especially used in the figure of speech called Anaphora, and particularly when the pronouns are repeated (<ab>e.g.</ab> <s>tám u stuṣa índram tám gṛṇīṣe</s> [<ls>RV. ii, 20, 4</ls>], him I praise, <s1 slp1="indra">Indra</s1>, him I sing). It may be used in drawing a conclusion, like the English ‘now’ (<ab>e.g.</ab> <s>tád u táthā ná kuryāt</s> [<ls>ŚBr. v, 2, 2, 3</ls>], that now he should not do in such a manner), and is frequently found in interrogative sentences (<ab>e.g.</ab> <s>ká u tác ciketa</s> [<ls>RV. i, 164, 48</ls>], who, I ask, should know that?)

NEW	 ¦ This particle may serve to give emphasis, like <s>id</s> and <s>eva</s>, especially after prepositions or demonstrative pronouns, in conjunction with <s>nu</s>, <s>vai</s>, <s>hi</s>, <s>cid</s>, &c. (<ab>e. g.</ab> <s>ayám u vām purutámo</s> … <s>johavīti</s> [<ls>RV. iii, 62, 2</ls>], this very person [your worshipper] invokes you &c.) It is especially used in the figure of speech called Anaphora, and particularly when the pronouns are repeated (<ab>e. g.</ab> <s>tám u stuṣa índram tám gṛṇīṣe</s> [<ls>RV. ii, 20, 4</ls>], him I praise, <s1>Indra</s1>, him I sing). It may be used in drawing a conclusion, like the <lang>English</lang> ‘now’ (<ab>e. g.</ab> <s>tád u táthā ná kuryāt</s> [<ls>ŚBr. v, 2, 2, 3</ls>], that now he should not do in such a manner), and is frequently found in interrogative sentences (<ab>e. g.</ab> <s>ká u tác ciketa</s> [<ls>RV. i, 164, 48</ls>], who, I ask, should know that?)
